  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6857b50b-c0d9-4c54-a6a3-08525299f5bd'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText15341754817881943810" style="display:none"><i>Can true love be</i> FORGOTTEN?<br /><br />As the only Scion who can descend into the Underworld, Helen Hamilton has been given a nearly impossible task. By night she wanders through Hades, trying to stop the endless cycle of revenge that has cursed her family. By day she struggles to overcome the fatigue that is rapidly eroding her sanity. Without Lucas by her side, Helen is not sure she has the strength to go on.<br /><br />Just as Helen is pushed to her breaking point, a mysterious new Scion comes to her rescue. Funny and brave, Orion shields her from the dangers of the Underworld. But time is running out - a ruthless foe plots against them, and the Furies' cry for blood is growing louder.<br /><br />As the ancient Greek world collides with the mortal one, Helen's sheltered life on Nantucket descends into chaos. But the hardest task of all will be forgetting Lucas Delos.<br /><br />Josephine Angelini's compelling saga becomes ever more intricate and spellbinding as an unforgettable love triangle emerges and the eternal cycle of revenge intensifies. Eagerly awaited, this sequel to the internationally bestselling STARCROSSED delivers a gritty, action-packed love story that exceeds all expectations.</span>

<div id="review_178141358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178141358" />
    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348368292p2/1235083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178141358?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabelle" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle">Annabelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=books-that-made-me-cry">books-that-made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=gorgeous-cover">gorgeous-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=signed-by-author">signed-by-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=cliffhangers">cliffhangers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178141358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3929628446686091038">****FINAL RATING: 3.60 STARS****<br/><br/><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br/>I loved Dreamless so much more than Starcrossed, although I was still disappointed with several aspects of it unfortunately. Still, it was an excellent read and I genuinely enjoyed it. I felt that it was an extremely well-done second installment and I was especially impressed by the character development.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>THE HEROINE</u>
</b><br/><u>HELEN</u><br/>Helen grows a lot in this book. Unfortunately, it's a rather slow growth, and it takes a while to really get into it. She starts o</span>
  <span id="freeText3929628446686091038" style="display:none">****FINAL RATING: 3.60 STARS****<br /><br /><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br />I loved Dreamless so much more than Starcrossed, although I was still disappointed with several aspects of it unfortunately. Still, it was an excellent read and I genuinely enjoyed it. I felt that it was an extremely well-done second installment and I was especially impressed by the character development.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE HEROINE</u>
</b><br /><u>HELEN</u><br />Helen grows a lot in this book. Unfortunately, it's a rather slow growth, and it takes a while to really get into it. She starts out unsure and weak, just trying to make her way, even if she kills herself. She doesn't really know at first what to do; all she knows is that she has to keep going. Later, she acs beautifully and steps into her role and really takes charge. However, she is a but too impulsive and doesn't always think before her actions, and it's clear there will be consequences.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE LOVE INTERESTS</u>
</b><br /><u>LUCAS</u><br />Much as I loved Lucas in Starcrossed, I really wasn't sure for the longest time how I felt about him in this book. I didn't approve of one of his initial decisions. Sure, he was misguided, but it was still his choice. I didn't like at all what he chose to do, and knew there were other ways. Such as figure out they're not actually cousins. I still have no clue why none of the characters are smart enough to figure it out. Anyway. He had a pretty great plot twist that I found really cool.<br /><u>ORION</u><br />Mmm, now here's a character to love. He's beautiful, and I want one. He's such a neat character and he's so kind and sweet. He really wants to help Helen but he's more accepting and open than she is. He helps her figure out who she is and I couldn't help but tumble headfirst into love with him. He's strong and smart and does what needs to be done. He also has an air of mystery that surrounds him and I cannot wait to find out more about him!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>(SOME OF) THE OTHER SECONDARY CHARACTERS</u>
</b><br /><u>HECTOR</u><br />Hector has always been, and will always be, my absolutely most favorite character. He's so freaking hot, and besides, apparently gives amazing hugs, which I so want. In general, I just want him. I love his strength and his gentleness and the deep love he feels for his family. He's so brave, and never backs down. He's protective without being possessive. I completely adore him and would be totally satisfied if the entire book revolved around him dancing with seagulls. That's how much I love him.<br /><u>ZACK</u><br />I felt really sorry for Zack in this one, and was sad to see some of his choices but glad to see others. He really struggles, blurring the line of good vs evil, and that was really interesting to see. I loved being in his head and seeing what he was thinking.<br /><u>JASON</u><br />I love Jason too. I honestly don't even know why, I just do. He's awesome. And hot. And I love him for no apparent reason, but whatever.<br /><u>CLAIRE</u><br />Actually, I didn't like Claire at all in this book. I'm not suing she is one, but she kind of acted like a bitch and i really didn't like that. I was really disappointed in her character and that was saddening, since I loved her so much in Starcrossed.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE PLOT</u>
</b><br />The plot was epic, intense, and everything I could have hoped for!<br /><br />Although in actuality, it started off far too slowly for my taste, and I was quite disenchanted with that. I felt like it took quite a while to get into the actual story itself. I didn't really care for that too much.<br /><br />Also, this whole Helen-and-Lucas are cousins thing has got to stop before I punch someone. If you really love each other, it shouldn't matter whether you're related or not. Furthermore, they're not related, and I find it hard to believe that they're all that ridiculously dumb and none of them can figure it out.<br /><br />Still, once the plot really got going, it was completely awesome. I couldn't put it down. There were so many plot twists that I could never completely guess just what was going to happen next.<br /><br />I completely loved the concept and the intense action and everything that was going on, the creepiness and the mythology and the little details and everything. Perfection.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ROMANCE</u>
</b><br />In my dream world, Helen would ditch both Lucas and Orion and end up with Hector. Then again, if she doesn't want him, I'll take him. However, since she won't, the choices are Lucas and Orion. I'm actually not really sure what team I'm on for possibly the first time ever in my life. I have good reasons for both Lucas and Orion and negative reasons for both. The romance was so beautifully well-developed and there's such heartache. If I really had to choose, I'd probably--oh, come on, I can't choose! For the first time in my life, I don't have a team. It's so weird.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE WRITING</u>
</b><br />Josie's writing has gotten so much better since Starcrossed! I love the gorgeous descriptions and the inner voices of the characters. Their thoughts fit them so well. Told mainly from third person POV via Helen, there's actually quite a variety of characters that take turns narrating the story, which is really cool and definitely contributes to its general awesomeness. I loved how much the writing became so real and really felt myself drawn in to the story.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ENDING</u>
</b><br />The ending was, in one word, perfect. There was betrayal. There was death. There was drama. There was love. There was war. There was resolution. There was everything I want to see at the end of a book and more, even better things. It was completely amazing and wrapped up the book beautifully, while leaving just enough unanswered and undone for the third book. Everything that had happened earlier in the book clicked together nicely.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>WRAUP</u>
</b><br />This book was so much better than Starcrossed, and I look forward to reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7849034.Goddess__Starcrossed___3_" title="Goddess (Starcrossed, #3) by Josephine Angelini" rel="nofollow noopener">Goddess</a> immensely! I am sure that the conclusion will be explosive and almost too awesome to be real, and I am ridiculously excited. Josie is showing real promise as an author, and I can't wait to see what she brings us next!<br /><br />FINE.<br /><br /><br />Read more of my reviews on <a href="http://sparkles-and-lightning.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sparkles and Lightning</a>!<br /><br />~<br /><br /><i>My pre-review</i><br /><br />I want this book now!! Lucas and Helen have to be together!!<br /><br />Oh, oh my God! What a breathlessly beautiful cover! I'm speechless.<br /><br />BUT WAIT. A LOVE TRIANGLE?!?!?!? ARE YOU FREAKING KIDDING ME?!?!?!?!? I AM SOOOOOOOO FREAKING SICK OF LOVE TRIANGLES!!!!!!! I AM OFFICIALLY TICKED OFF. That's it. Someone is dying.<br /><br />But I'll still eagerly await the book, albeit somewhat more annoyedly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3929628446686091038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8598022437190735612" style="display:none"><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/despicableme.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Hold on a sec while I pick my jaw up off the floor…<br><br><b> WOW! </b><br><br>I’m suffering from one GARGANTUAN (love that word) book hangover. Seriously, I’m a mess. You can’t see me right now, but my hair is doing that I’ve-never-heard-of-a-brush thing, and my clothes are direly craving the ironing board (that I never use), and my emotions are off somewhere crying in a corner begging for a shot or bottle of Tequila.<br><br>And the buttprint on my very comfy couch is getting larger. I’d like to think that the largeness of said buttprint is caused by my not getting off of it for the past couple of days and <i>not</i> the even *larger* gargantuan amounts of chocolate I’ve consumed at the expense of my emotional meltdowns brought on by THIS book.<br><br>Because it’s just that awesome. ;)<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_mkp3zb9Tdf1qbeln5o1_500_zpsda2f7815.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>_______________________________________<br><br>And just to warn you that while you read this…<br><br><b>You <i>will</i> be doin’ a little bit of this:</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/crying2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_634242615" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/634242615" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/634242615?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634242615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10099136576892888598"><b>"'Please,' she sobbed quietly. 'Just kill me now.'"</b><br/><br/>Oh, Helen, my dear. I would if I could, if only so this book could end sooner and I didn't have to suffer through a month of reading it.<br/><br/>The main thing I can recall about reading this book is that it was so incredibly boring. It took me so long reading it, trudging through it by bits and pieces at a time because it was so completely, utterly unabsorbing. I'm always amazed at how a plot-driven book can be so dull, but this book proves that it can </span>
  <span id="freeText10099136576892888598" style="display:none"><b>"'Please,' she sobbed quietly. 'Just kill me now.'"</b><br /><br />Oh, Helen, my dear. I would if I could, if only so this book could end sooner and I didn't have to suffer through a month of reading it.<br /><br />The main thing I can recall about reading this book is that it was so incredibly boring. It took me so long reading it, trudging through it by bits and pieces at a time because it was so completely, utterly unabsorbing. I'm always amazed at how a plot-driven book can be so dull, but this book proves that it can be done. Everything I loved about the first book was nonexistent in the second. I should be able to say more about a book of this length, of this depth, that requires so much of an investment in time but I just can't. It's about 50% longer than it needed to be.<br /><br />For a book of this length, it has a surprising lack of depth. Some books have such complexity of plot that I can hardly sum it up in a page without feeling like I'm leaving out some minor but utterly essential segment of the plot. This book suffers from no such problems. I can summarize it in one sentence and you probably wouldn't miss much. Helen goes to the Underworld nightly, and tries to solve the mystery of...something on the grand scale of wars between the gods and the mysteries of the Furies and shit. Every day. Repeat for weeks. That is the entire book. I don't even know anymore. The plot is just bogged down with unnecessary teenage angst and the overall lengthiness just muddles up the plot so much that I don't even know what's going on.<br /><br />Second book syndrome, thy name is <i>Dreamless</i>.<br /><br /><u>Some things I loved in the first book that went down the crapper in the sequel</u>:<br />1. TWOO WUV: First book: Ok, a tad clichéd. Fine, very clichéd, but I like the straightforwardness of it. Romeo &amp; Juliet plot, Lucas and Helen can't be together, but they're devoted to each other and each other alone. Fine with me, I'm all for that. Second book: half-assed love triangle.<br /><br />Lucas: I CAN'T LOVE YOU BECAUSE IT'S NOT FATED FOR US. Therefore I shall pretend to hate you and make you hate me by being absolutely deplorable and an altogether despicable piece of shit and do stupid things like beat up my own father because I can't have whom I want! Wah!!!!!<br /><br />Helen: LUCAAAAAAAAAAAAS. WHY ARE YOU LIKE THIS? I LOVE YOU. I know we're cousins and that's totally gross but we're meant to be together so why are you being such a jer---Why hello there, handsome, what's your name?<br /><br />Orion: I'm Orion! I'm gorgeous and I hold a bunch of titles and I've got Aphrodite's blessings, I'm perfect!<br /><br />Lucas: Sup dude :(<br /><br />Orion: Yo, man. :|<br /><br />Helen: BUT I LIKE YOU BOTH D:<br /><br />Lucas + Orion: Ok<br /><br />2. Characterization: First book: loved it. Helen's character turned from stupid silly Mary Sue to someone I could actually sympathize with. Second book...not so much. What leftover sympathy I had for Helen from the first book disappeared quickly. She does not change at all within the book. Still blaming herself for everything, still making mistakes, still taking on too much, and now, she's even more of a martyr. Same with Lucas, same with the rest of the cast, really. This book is heavily plot-driven, and considering the plot is weak, it fails in keeping my interest because of the lack of character development. The newly introduced characters are similarly flat. Orion is the gorgeous (aren't they all) golden boy, with a tragic past, but always with a smile on his face to hide his pain! Clichéd, clichéd, clichéd. Automedon is a mindless bot, out to kill. You could call Automedon "the Terminator" instead, and it wouldn't be too much of a stretch. Well, besides for the fact that the Terminator had more personality.<br /><br />And Hector. THERE IS A SERIOUS LACK OF HECTOR HERE. I'm not talking about his presence, considering it's bound to be lacking considering his exiled status, but his personality. The take-no-prisoner attitude is gone, the no-nonsense attitude is gone, there's no telling Helen to suck it up and be who she was meant to be. Hector's gone <i>soft</i> on us, people.<br /><br />3. Random-ass plot: First book: heavily mythology-driven, well-explained history of the Houses, good basis of Greek mythology that's not too far-fetched from anything you can find in Bullfinch's. Second book, let's throw everything into the mix, let's screw up the gods and goddesses and make them into random creatures that fit the plot, rather than the other way around. The inaccurate depictions of the myths and the gods and goddesses here bring to mind <i>The Goddess Test</i> and we all know how much I absolute <i>loved</i> that book. /end sarcasm<br /><br /><b>"'Ares,' Orion whispered to Helen over his shoulder as the god skipped off, giggling hysterically, to hide among the bones. 'Don't be afraid, Helen. He's a coward.'<br />'He's insane!' Helen whispered back frantically. 'He’s completely and totally insane!'"</b><br /><br />Ares? The god of war? <i>Really?</i><br /><br />By the end of the book, I don't even know what the plot is anymore, what started off fairly simply in book one turned out to be a convoluted mess in book 2, and I honestly have no idea what the big mystery that they're all fussing over is due to the gigantic mess that became the backbone of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10099136576892888598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_135754751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135754751" />
    <a title="hayden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden"><img alt="hayden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598996671p2/2995566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135754751?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hayden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hayden" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden">hayden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=hurry-up-and-get-published">hurry-up-and-get-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2995566-hayden?shelf=own-arc-want-finished">own-arc-want-finished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135754751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4657900591284637949">Google, define "sophomore slump" for me, please.<br/><blockquote>"A sophomore slump or sophomore jinx refers to an instance in which a second, or sophomore, effort fails to live up to the standards of the first effort."</blockquote><br/>Ladies and gentlemen, <b>this is the antithesis of a sophomore slump.</b> Angelini steps up the action and the passion and the sizzling tension in DREAMLESS; in fact, <b>breathing isn't an option</b>. You'll be holding the air in your lungs and turning pages faster than you can believe.<br/>Helen Hamilton just can't</span>
  <span id="freeText4657900591284637949" style="display:none">Google, define "sophomore slump" for me, please.<br /><blockquote>"A sophomore slump or sophomore jinx refers to an instance in which a second, or sophomore, effort fails to live up to the standards of the first effort."</blockquote><br />Ladies and gentlemen, <b>this is the antithesis of a sophomore slump.</b> Angelini steps up the action and the passion and the sizzling tension in DREAMLESS; in fact, <b>breathing isn't an option</b>. You'll be holding the air in your lungs and turning pages faster than you can believe.<br />Helen Hamilton just can't catch a break. She needs to descend into the Underworld, since she's the only one who can, and find the Furies to complete a mission she's been set on . . . but she can't control her descents and she finds herself in random and painful scenarios. She meets someone in the fiery pits of Hell named Orion.<br /><b>A fierce love triangle emerges </b>from the darkness. Helen and Lucas are taking a break, since something happened in Starcrossed and led to them breaking apart, but Helen can't keep her mind off of him.<br />Helen enters the Underworld in her dreams. At the beginning of the novel, I wasn't thinking this was how it was going to happen and when I found out it was, I was instantly relieved. I wasn't looking forward to a long, grueling journey where the heroine would be away from everyone in Nantucket for so long. The way Angelini did this was great.<br /><b>And can I say now how much I just love the cover?! </b>Whoever designed this cover needs a raise, because I am barely able to look at that book without mentally swooning.<br />Dreamless is the first HarperCollins ARC I've ever read, and it was definitely a great start.<br /><b>With rich mythology and a passionate love triangle, DREAMLESS takes the intensity up to a whole new level! Be prepared to be swept off your feet.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4657900591284637949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review135754751">

Moreover, author introduced new character and created love triangle. A big no-no for me!</b><br><br>My Lucas, Helen and Orion:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386958346i/7492847.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is excellent example of how to ruin series which had plenty of potential. I forced myself to finish but I did not enjoy it. And now I do not care what is going to happen or with whom heroine is going to end up with. I am very disappointed since I liked first book a lot and now I decided not to even be bothered to finish this series.<br><br>MORE REVIEWS ON MY BLOG <a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2447376323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447376323" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78730059-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545995679p2/78730059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447376323?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/78730059-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447376323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11933431347610164824">3,5 stars<br/><br/>“It's not our talents that make us safe or dangerous, it's our choices.”<br/><br/>I have so many things to say about this book since my opinion about the whole series changed from negative-ish to positive. I have no idea how to rate this book, no more than 4 stars for sure, but 3 stars seems too low since Dreamless was better than Starcrossed in so many aspects.<br/><br/>Plot picks up where Starcossed left it. Helen keeps descending to Uderworld in order to stop the furies while rest of the Delos family tr</span>
  <span id="freeText11933431347610164824" style="display:none">3,5 stars<br /><br />“It's not our talents that make us safe or dangerous, it's our choices.”<br /><br />I have so many things to say about this book since my opinion about the whole series changed from negative-ish to positive. I have no idea how to rate this book, no more than 4 stars for sure, but 3 stars seems too low since Dreamless was better than Starcrossed in so many aspects.<br /><br />Plot picks up where Starcossed left it. Helen keeps descending to Uderworld in order to stop the furies while rest of the Delos family try to help her as best as they can. She can’t get in contact with her mysterious mother Daphne who pops in her life only when she has something important to add, but at least she helps her by sending Orion- double Heir with artifact that enables him to descend with Helen. Her best friends Claire and Matt start getting involved with Scions and Helen’s dangerous life and protecting them becomes harder every day. Since descending prevents her to sleep, Helen becomes more exhausted every day her relationship with Lucas is going to hell and on top of everything, major part of the House Thebes wants her dead. <br /><br />Although I didn’t like world building and abilities demigods inherit trough the first book, I started to ignore the fact that there was not specific way of inheriting certain powers and rather enjoyed connections with Greek gods and their abilities. Parallels with Greek mythology were explained and deepened and many things made more sense. For example, Helen’s descending was much clearer and easier to grasp and imagine. Everything about Houses, Outcasts and Rogues was thoroughly explained, rather than just stating prophecies and confusing facts or concepts that have been briefly mentioned in conversation. <br /><br />This is probably just me, but I could sense obvious improvement in writing style. It felt like narrative was flowing more naturally and dialogues stopped being forced in some kind of weird slang. <br /><br />Even though I am used to second book in trilogy being the most non-dynamic, this wasn’t the case. Plot was way more intense and dynamic than the first book and there was always something happening. It had just the right amount of twists, descriptions and endangering characters to entertain the reader. After half of the book I couldn’t stop reading and the ending was intense and unpredictable with much tension and opening for an amazing finish in last book of the trilogy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ After Ares freed other gods from the Olympus and started a war, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ there is a lot of potential for Goddess and plot itself.<br /><br />Helen Hamilton remained perfect, beautiful, but plain and boring character. She got a little bit more interesting, but only because of the plot and other characters who contributed o her development. Something I loved about her was her determination to take care of her family and friends no matter the cost. Other times I didn’t particularly care for her, except when she whined about Lucas which annoyed me to pieces. She also seems to be happy to die all the time- every time she was near death she stopped fighting and, literally, begged to die. <br /><br />Aaaand after 20 pages of the book, there it is! Love triangle. It would have been so much better if Angelini just killed of Lucas. He is such unnecessary character with no other considerable traits than being handsome. I like Orion because he actually has some backstory and hope he and Helen will be endgame. I really hope there won’t be any love triangle drama in Goddess because I can’t take it. <br />Also, is everyone there dense not to notice Helen is 17 and Ajax died 19 years ago?<br />As for other characters, they stayed pretty much the same- likable and heroic, but not to complex. I am glad to see some other relationships and developments that aren’t Helen’s.<br /><br />If you have read Starcrossed and have doubts about continuing it, do it. I can say it gets better and more enjoyable and as far as I have seen, Goddess is even better :) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="11933431347610164824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

IM BEGGING YOU JOSIE, PLEASE NO MORE LOVE TRIANGLES... Many fans (including myself) are getting really tired of it..."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15957859148475657713">The start of this book was actually OK, for the first 10 pages or so and then it went down hill. So... Let's try something different here...<br/><br/>***<br/><br/>Hi, my name's Helen. I am the absolutely STUNNING AND PERFECT LOOKING protagonist of this book. In fact, I'm the most freaking beautiful girl in the world. No joke. The face that launched a thousand ships and all that. Doesn't matter that beauty is subject to the eyes of the beholder and different cultures have different definitions of beautiful.<br/><br/>Last book</span>
  <span id="freeText15957859148475657713" style="display:none">The start of this book was actually OK, for the first 10 pages or so and then it went down hill. So... Let's try something different here...<br /><br />***<br /><br />Hi, my name's Helen. I am the absolutely STUNNING AND PERFECT LOOKING protagonist of this book. In fact, I'm the most freaking beautiful girl in the world. No joke. The face that launched a thousand ships and all that. Doesn't matter that beauty is subject to the eyes of the beholder and different cultures have different definitions of beautiful.<br /><br />Last book, I fell in LURVE with Lucas but then was told that he's my cousin but I still want to get it on with him. Like, really badly. My lips pucker at the sight of him and everything.<br /><br />Oh, but look! Someone new! Hi there, Orion, I think I fancy you now. Mmmhhmmm.<br /><br />Everyone keeps telling me that I'm so skinny I look like I should be sectioned. It's not my fault I go down to the underworld every night and walk for days and days and end up getting hurt and this all means that my body needs more energy. And it's SO not my fault that I'd rather dick around flying in the sky than have my dinner after having only some pancakes for breakfast and a sandwich after school. It's not my fault I'm skinny and I wish everyone would get off my back about eating even though I don't eat.<br /><br />Oh, and I'm falling behind in my school work because I literally don't sleep and I rarely eat. And I don't have time to do my homework cause I'd rather be pissing around flying. But don't worry, I'm not bottom of the class or anything. I'm Mary Sue. I mean, I'm Helen. How could I be <i>bottom</i> of the class?<br /><br />Oh, did I mention that I'm also immensely powerful? But I don't know it. Or course. I mean, if I knew I was so powerful and actually used the power, I'd be a slightly more complex character rather than a bland-as-paint-drying-Mary-Sue.<br /><br />***<br /><br />Yeah, I didn't like this book. I mean, I quite liked Helen's torture at the beginning. That was interesting. But I definitely did not like her woe-is-me-everyone's-getting-at-me-and-it's-not-my-fault-blah-blah-blah selfish yet selfless personality. Urgh. Grow up, eat a freaking sandwich and get your priorities right you selfish little child.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this for free via Goodreads First Reads.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15957859148475657713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer303683071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3842360707472248620">***NOTE! review is posted on <a href='http://jacitamati.blogspot.com/2012/05/dreamless-starcrossed-2-by-josephine.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ja čitam, a ti?</a><br/><br/><br/> Are you, Jose Angelini, one of the descendants of, um, I don't know... Is there Greek goddess of torturing by cliffhangers? Just to make one thing clear - I wouldn't mind if you leave the love story as it is. Yes, I am that kinky.<br/><br/> Second book in Starcrossed series picks up where first one ended so maybe it would be good idea if you refresh your memory before you start reading. Dreamless is more focused on Helen's role in the new world she found hersel</span>
  <span id="freeText3842360707472248620" style="display:none">***NOTE! review is posted on <a href="http://jacitamati.blogspot.com/2012/05/dreamless-starcrossed-2-by-josephine.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ja čitam, a ti?</a><br /><br /><br /> Are you, Jose Angelini, one of the descendants of, um, I don't know... Is there Greek goddess of torturing by cliffhangers? Just to make one thing clear - I wouldn't mind if you leave the love story as it is. Yes, I am that kinky.<br /><br /> Second book in Starcrossed series picks up where first one ended so maybe it would be good idea if you refresh your memory before you start reading. Dreamless is more focused on Helen's role in the new world she found herself part of. Don't be disappointed, there's going to be lot of emotional tensions - all suckers for romance will be really happy because there's a new boy. And he's not just any boy - I'm still in team Lucas, now even more than before: good boy is seriously gone bad. Actually, all characters are darker and whole book has this gothic feeling especially parts about the Underworld. But I have to admit one thing. I love strong and believable female characters more than hot, bad, bookish boys and Helen is definitely in this group.<br /><br /> I think that even if you didn't enjoyed that much in the first book, you are going to devour this one. All the things I found lacking in the Starcrossed is set on the right path in sequel. Josepine Angelini is growing up as the author and I think I have a new girl crush (latest one was on Tara Kelly). Speaking about Josephine, check out her blog post <a href="http://www.josephineangelini.com/blog/2012/05/writing/photos-v-imagination/" rel="nofollow noopener">Photos vs Imagination</a> - is it good thing to put faces on the covers and how does it influence the way readeres imagine characters. One more reason why I like this girl so much. What do you think? Do you agree with Josephine?</span>

<div id="review_419413269" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419413269" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419413269?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419413269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12991102634420298833">To see full review click here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/2013/01/dreamless-josephine-angelini.html'>http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/201...</a><br/><br/>Screw the format I usually follow.<br/><br/>I can't do it today. Not after I read this rainbow turd of a book. That's right, I said rainbow turd. And when I say rainbow turd, you know the book's shitty. If you don't want to read my entire rant about why Dreamless was even more insipid than its shitty predecessor, I'll briefly summarize why I hated it: it was way too long, the character is on the same Mary Sue level as Bethany Church, a</span>
  <span id="freeText12991102634420298833" style="display:none">To see full review click here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/2013/01/dreamless-josephine-angelini.html">http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/201...</a><br /><br />Screw the format I usually follow.<br /><br />I can't do it today. Not after I read this rainbow turd of a book. That's right, I said rainbow turd. And when I say rainbow turd, you know the book's shitty. If you don't want to read my entire rant about why Dreamless was even more insipid than its shitty predecessor, I'll briefly summarize why I hated it: it was way too long, the character is on the same Mary Sue level as Bethany Church, and I've seen more coherent plots come out of Power Rangers.<br /><br />So I guess now, I'm going to start my rant. I thought a lot about how I was going to address my issues with this book. But maybe I'm not the best person to address how foul this unicorn rainbow barf/fart is. That's why I'm leaving that job to Helen.<br /><br />Yes, I'm letting Helen freaking Heavenly Hamilton tell you why this book sucks. Well, actually I'm going to be interviewing her (don't worry, I've taken proper precautions-mojitos).<br /><br />Me: So, Helen, we meet again.<br /><br />Helen: Aren't you going to tell me how beyoutiful I am?<br /><br />Me: You look like a Barbie. But I really don't care about how you look.<br /><br />Helen: But I'm the face. Everyone looooooooooooooovvvvvvvvveeeeeeeeeeesssss.....<br /><br />Me: Shut up.<br /><br />Helen: Gasp! What did you tell me?<br /><br /><br />Me: I said to shut up. I honestly, don't get it. Why everyone bows down to you? When you're one of the most useless characters in YA literature.<br /><br />Helen: I thought that went to Bethany Church or that Luce girl<br /><br />Me (groans): They're annoying too. But I just spent a week reading about your shitty glitter antics and how you never have consequences to deal with. And how your freaking perfect and how all the boys love you. And how anyone who doesn't is an evil person....Jesus, can't you give it a rest.<br /><br />Helen: I didn't think I did anything wrong. And I can't help it that I have the face.<br /><br />Me: Oh, you can help it. You can start by not being so useless. Or maybe taking responsibility for your actions and not solving every problem (like the furies) like a freaking bad Saturday morning cartoon.<br /><br />Helen: Cartoons are for babies.<br /><br />Me: Um, no they're not. There's actually a lot of really good cartoons that I still watch as an adult. But your whole story reads like a bad cartoon. The solution to your problems is way too easy. There's no character development between you and any of the characters.<br /><br />Helen: But what about Orion?<br /><br />Me: You mean the replacement Lucas that you instantly fell in love with. When he was suppose to, I don't know help you fight the furies.<br /><br />Helen: He's not a replacement for Lucas. Lucas is...ew, he's my cousin.<br /><br />Me (rolls eyes): You know, it's still legal to marry your cousin in a lot of the US (including Massachusetts which is where your from), right? It's not the same thing as dating your brother (looks in the direction of Clary Fray) though it's not exactly what I'd consider...The point is, it's legal and considered normal by many people. It's not that taboo.<br /><br />Helen: But we'll end up like Oedipus.<br /><br />Me: Hmmm, unless Lucas's dad went back in time and was either Lucas or Orion then I don't think you could be his own mother. And God, you're still thinking about him. Them. Why can't you like do something constructive like learn to fight?<br /><br />Helen: I don't mean to be useless it's not my fault that I'm powerless in the underworld.<br /><br />Me: (skeptical look) Didn't you sort of blow off Hector in the last book? And that's another thing I don't get, if you're supposedly related to him why didn't you want to kill him....<br /><br />Helen: Um, I'm a special snowflake who doesn't like being special.<br /><br />Me: Of course you are.<br /><br />Helen: Was that sarcasm?<br /><br />Me (Acting innocent): Of course not. Though I do have to admit you're a bit of a dumb ass by now if...<br /><br />Helen: If what....<br /><br />Me: Spoilers.<br /><br />Helen: But I want to know?<br /><br />Me: Moving on....<br /><br />Helen: Hey! I want to know.<br /><br />Me: This is my interview, Helen. Now I want to talk about that ludicrous plot of yours. Did your author take an acid trip when she read Edith Hamilton's Mythology?<br /><br />Helen: That's mean.<br /><br />Me: Well, I'm sorry. I'm just making a generalization, I just don't understand the concept of Angelini's world building. Then again, I can't figure out why she'd get a seven figure deal for this shit fest. Heck....<br /><br />Helen: What's so bizarre about the story? It uses Greek mythology, right?<br /><br />Me: More like it has rainbow and glitter diarrhea all over Greek Mythology.<br /><br />Helen (crosses arms): It does not.<br /><br />Me: Okay, does this make sense to you: Emo teen who can go in the underworld without being dead or a dignity every night dying because she can't dream (rolls eyes on this one), emo teenage boy we're suppose to find hot who beats up things because he can't bang his cousin, some scions from different houses hating each other some not, magic rivers with special river juice, ant men who aren't a part of the Marvel universe, furies who no longer try to kill you even before you give them river juice, people being more afraid of people with invisibility powers than girls who can shoot lightening out of their hands, having people go to school after they crash their bike into sewage water and touch a dead animal that could've been rabid....<br /><br />Helen: Hey, that last one doesn't have to deal with the world building.<br /><br />Me: That last one was just there because it was gross. Seriously, any self respecting human being would've headed home or better yet the hospital after touching dead squirrel. For all you know it could've had rabies or some other wild animal disease. And to go to school like that? Do you really want to be known as Rotten Rodent Girl?<br /><br /><br />Helen: But it was school...<br /><br />Me: You weren't there and once you got a pass, you basically skipped the whole day anyway. And I used this particular example because it was really gross and unnecessary just about like the rest of the 480 pages of this book. Seriously, it could've been cut in half and it still would've been too long.<br /><br />Helen: You just hated it because I'm beautiful.<br /><br />Me: No. No. I got annoyed that I kept hearing how pretty you are. But I could care less about your looks. Honestly, I thought it was sort of cool that Helen of Troy was your archetype at first because you could've been a real bitch of a character. But nope...you're perfect annoyingly squeaky clean Helen. And I hate you. Heck, Angelini can't even do archetypes right....it's not even like she knows the characters. Like Paris, he's not suppose to be the hero.<br /><br />Helen: Paris?<br /><br />Me: Lucas. But your author renamed him, probably because calling a guy Paris isn't going to make him sound like Edward Cullen which is what I think she was striving towards. Honestly, I have to wonder if this series was originally fan fiction. I mean, it's pitched like it's Percy Jackson for girls. Lucas is a rip off for Edward with his controlling and stalkerish ways. Seriously, he sits in front of your bedroom all night that's not right, and you two are broken up in book two just like Bella and Edward. Oh, and you know have a lightening bolt scar like Harry freaking Potter. And Orion could just as well be a teenage Sirius Black.<br /><br />Helen: Are you finished?<br /><br />Me: No, quite frankly I'm not. Seven fucking figures. Seven fucking figures. Do you know what I could do with that sort of advance. And it's not even like she tried with this piece of unicorn poo. Even my fan fictions are better than this....this fucking piece of....<br /><br />Helen: Hey! What about the other characters?<br /><br />Me: What?<br /><br />Helen: You're not complaining about them....<br /><br />Me: Oh, I'm not. I already mentioned that she loves archetypes didn't I? That all of you scions are based very loosely off of Greek figures. Oh, did I also mention that she's generalized all the supportive human roles too. Let's see, while there is some diversity in these books the characters are token characters at best like Claire (or Giggles if we're using your stupid nickname for her). And while that by itself is great, we're told that Claire is sort of weary about dating guys who aren't the same race as her (i.e. she's in love with Jason). And we're told this is a tradition. WTF!??!!?!?! Oh, and if that little generalization isn't bad enough, the Latina characters in this book are described frequently as saucy. Note to authors writing diverse characters, just because their skin color/culture/background is different than yours we don't have to generalize them by describing them as saucy or having their relatives frown when they bring their non-Japanese boyfriend/friends home for dinner and have that character contemplate about dumping a guy just based off of skin color. Fucking unicorn sparkly..........<br /><br />Helen: Can you just shut up already.<br /><br />Me: No, I had to put up with you for a week and....<br /><br />Helen: (lightening bolt forms from her hand) Seriously, shut up now...<br /><br />Me: You're too much of a Mary Sue to do it (grabs water gun from purse and sprays Helen. Helen falls to the floor withering and claiming that she's melting). Wrong book. Now that that nonsense is done. I think it's time I read another book, something that makes me retain my faith in humanity. Seven fucking figures.....<br /><br />* Note, for those who don't know I am not Josephine Angelini. I do not own the character Helen. I merely using her character to review this God forsaken unicorn puke book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12991102634420298833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1950760776" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1950760776" />
    <a title="Caylynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn"><img alt="Caylynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594527171p2/66237296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1950760776?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caylynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caylynn" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn">Caylynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1950760776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13051753831679500982"><i>
  <b>Re-re-reread review!</b>
</i><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>These visits to the parts of the Underworld where she was in no immediate danger lasted the longest and ended up being the hardest in the long run... Hell didn't need lakes of fire to torment. Time and solitude were enough.</blockquote>
</i><br/>Me every time I reread this trilogy-<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490880806ra/22354486.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Seriously. I fucking love this trilogy SO MUCH. It is one of those extremely rare ones where the sequel is just as good as (and some rereads <i>even better than</i>) the first installment, and I know every time I dive in</span>
  <span id="freeText13051753831679500982" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Re-re-reread review!</b>
</i><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>These visits to the parts of the Underworld where she was in no immediate danger lasted the longest and ended up being the hardest in the long run... Hell didn't need lakes of fire to torment. Time and solitude were enough.</blockquote>
</i><br>Me every time I reread this trilogy-<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490880806ra/22354486.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously. I fucking love this trilogy SO MUCH. It is one of those extremely rare ones where the sequel is just as good as (and some rereads <i>even better than</i>) the first installment, and I know every time I dive into the story that I'm going to fall in love with it all over again.<br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12995284.Dreamless__Starcrossed___2_" title="Dreamless (Starcrossed, #2) by Josephine Angelini" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreamless</a>, Helen and the Delos family are dealing with the fallout of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9462795.Starcrossed__Starcrossed___1_" title="Starcrossed (Starcrossed, #1) by Josephine Angelini" rel="nofollow noopener">Starcrossed</a>. Hector is an Outcast, Lucas and Helen have <i>yet another</i> reason as to why fate won't allow them to be together, the family is preparing for an all out war, and Helen now has to deal with the crushing responsibility of being the only demigod who can descend into the Underworld to fulfill the quest of freeing all demigods from the Furies and their rage-inducing blood oaths. <br><br>I don't know what it is about Josephine Angelini's writing, but it is so <i>easy</i> to feel <i>everything</i> that Helen is suffering through throughout this novel. The themes of depression and involuntary isolation are heavy as hell in the sequel, and in comparison to the upbeat tempo of Helen discovering what she is and finding a group of people that eventually become like family to her in the first book, it hits you <i>hard</i>.<br><i>
  <blockquote>Helen glanced around her room. The silence pounded in her ears and the walls spiraled in on her. She didn't want to be the Descender anymore... <br><br>She was at the end of her endurance. She was beyond tired, but couldn't let herself fall asleep in this condition. If she did, she didn't know if she would ever have the strength to wake up again.</blockquote>
</i><br>As someone with severe depression when I first read this trilogy, I connected so hard with everything Helen thought about in these scenes of solitude. My favorite thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12995284.Dreamless__Starcrossed___2_" title="Dreamless (Starcrossed, #2) by Josephine Angelini" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreamless</a> is the way that Angelini approaches the failures of a hero, and how those failures are taken a <i>lot</i> more seriously by the other characters than if another, lesser character had committed them. You've seen it in <i>Harry Potter</i>. You've seen it in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a>. You've even seen it in fucking <i>Avatar:TLA</i>. Our lovable (most of the time) hero makes one slip up-no matter the size- and the others all pounce on it like they're lions in a fighting pit. The amount of times that Helen is bullied and pushed back and forth for things that <s>sometimes</s> aren't even her fault gets to the point where you just want to reach in and shake all the characters for their idiocy. <br><br>But, of course, we can't talk about all the depressing shit without bringing up the shining ball of light that is Orion. The new guy on the block, Orion is <i>literally</i> Helen's saving grace as she's suffering through the deepest depths of Tartarus. He actually succeeds in making her laugh as they're trudging through hell itself.<br><i>
  <blockquote>“After all, the monsters think you're the delicious one."<br><br>"Smart monsters. I AM tasty."<br><br>"Says who?"<br><br>"Don't believe me? See for yourself."<br><br>"Yeah? How?"<br><br>"Bite me.” </blockquote>
</i><br>He is EASILY my favorite character in the entire trilogy. SWOON.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468115804ra/19668328.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But really though, Orion is the friend/something else that <i>everyone</i> needs during their bad days.<br><br>I'm going to end this review before I gush even more than I already have by saying...READ THIS TRILOGY ASAP IF YOU HAVEN'T ALREADY, DAMN IT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13051753831679500982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_270943021" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270943021" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4979538-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520654483p2/4979538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270943021?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/4979538-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=tbr-on-ipad">tbr-on-ipad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270943021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2859686411152647345">*****3.5 stars*******<br/><br/>Okay, so this is a toughie for me. I am a huge Starcrossed fan, it is such a well-executed, thrilling story with characters that I just absolutely fell in love with. The wait for Dreamless was a long one, so I couldn't wait to dive right in the day it was released. Honestly, though, I found myself really struggling to get back into the story, and at about 20% in I had to shelf this one for a few weeks. I finally sat down today and finished it, and I was a little disappointed</span>
  <span id="freeText2859686411152647345" style="display:none">*****3.5 stars*******<br /><br />Okay, so this is a toughie for me. I am a huge Starcrossed fan, it is such a well-executed, thrilling story with characters that I just absolutely fell in love with. The wait for Dreamless was a long one, so I couldn't wait to dive right in the day it was released. Honestly, though, I found myself really struggling to get back into the story, and at about 20% in I had to shelf this one for a few weeks. I finally sat down today and finished it, and I was a little disappointed when I was done.<br /><br />The fact that the plot just didn't hold my interest was a big part of the issue. In the beginning of Dreamless, Helen is essentially just repeating the same process over and over again, going down to the underworld searching for the answer to stopping the furies. There wasn't a whole lot else going on, even with the secondary characters, so I just got bored with it. When Orion finally came into the picture, things started looking up a bit. Not b/c I was all that into his character, but it was a twist that I could latch onto. There was a lot of fact-sharing and history-revealing, but without any exciting action going on in the mean time, it was hard to keep interested. <br /><br />Then here's my biggest problem; the thing that I loved MOST about Starcrossed was the beautiful romance between Lucas and Helen, and I realized early on that their relationship (of any capacity) was just absent here. Yes, Starcrossed ended with them thinking they were cousins, so we all knew where this was going for awhile. But I didn't expect Lucas to just be gone from the story in the way he was in Dreamless. He was heartbroken and alone, and Helen was heartbroken and going through hell, but they hardly even speak to each other. It bothered me that all of the other characters just expected them to get over it, and just expected Helen to put herself through the nightly torture. Everyone acted as if they were just being asked to do these simple tasks, and when they struggled with them it was shameful. It made the whole situation even more hard to swallow for me. <br /><br />What saved this book for me was the last 25-30% of the story. There are plot twists and struggles with the enemies that kept me glued to the book, plus I FINALLY got what I'd been waiting for. Here, we finally see the return of the Lucas we all so dearly missed, the love that they share, and how amazing they are when they work together!!! He helps Helen finally sort things out in her head, and he's there for her to support her so she knows that she's not alone. THIS was what was missing in the first part of this book, and I was so very happy to have it back!!!! God, I just love Lucas!! I really ended up liking Orion in the second half of the book, too, despite my objections to Helen falling for him. It's so not fair to Lucas, but I didn't let that fact cloud my judgement of Orion. He's sweet, caring, brave, and drop-dead gorgeous, so it's hard to not love him!! =) <br /><br />Lucas and Helen by far make the greatest changes in Dreamless, and they both become much stronger and more confident in their strengths. Though Helen does doubt herself during her trips to the underworld, she keeps pushing through and pushing herself to the limit so that she can complete the task and save all of them from the furies. When the final battles come around, she once again finds the strength within herself to fight for all of them. I loved watching her get all bad-ass again, I hated seeing her run down and desperate. And Lucas, between his growing temper and newly developed abilities, is shaping up to be a force to be reckoned with in the future!! I'm miffed that he and Helen still don't know the truth at the end of Dreamless, and I worry what that will mean for him in the next book. I really hope they don't have to be in the dark much longer, I could just strangle Helen's mother for keeping the truth from them!!<br /><br />So, overall I wanted much more from a good portion of the book, but I thoroughly enjoyed the rest. I'm still a huge fan of the series and I very much look forward to reading Goddess next year!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2859686411152647345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11558083863936424667">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>Alright, so this book wasn't that bad. It was creepy and seriously stupid but apart from that, it was bearable. In the first book, Lucas and Helen were all laddi-da-da, totally in their "together forever" mode. Now, after they found out that they're ohmigosh, cousins! They can like never ever be together.   <span id="freeText11558083863936424667" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />Alright, so this book wasn't that bad. It was creepy and seriously stupid but apart from that, it was bearable. In the first book, Lucas and Helen were all laddi-da-da, totally in their "together forever" mode. Now, after they found out that they're ohmigosh, cousins! They can like never ever be together. Apart from the fact that IT'S COMPLETELY STUPID HOW NO ONE REALISED THAT IT'S IMPOSSIBLE. I have no idea what the hell happened. Lucas is missing for like literally half the f**king book. Idk what kind of shit he gets up to, just sitting and watching her like freaking Edward while she sleeps. Then he goes on and ignores her while she is clearly SUFFERING. She's practically getting frozen in her little iceberg of a bedroom, which btw i have no idea how her dad doesn't realise that it's like a freaking igloo or arctic shit in there. I mean what kind of parent doesn't at least poke their head in once to see how their kid is doing? I was surprised she didn't have to don snow gear and start shovelling out some ice because it had gotten to the point where her bedroom has become an ice rink.<br /><br />Then there was the other guy. OF COURSE THERE HAD TO BE ANOTHER GUY. I MEAN WHAT KIND OF TEEN ANGSTY BOOK WOULD IT BE WITHOUT A LOVE TRIANGLE? Another completely unoriginal and overused idea. The other reason it made me annoyed was that having one, made me really question how much she actually "loved" Lucas, and if she really did love him at all. Because as my god Johnny Depp said <i> "If you find yourself in love with two people, choose the second one, because if you really loved the first one you wouldn't have fallen for the second.” </i><br /><br />Okay, so maybe she doesn't really love Orion and the "excitement" she felt with him was just an excuse to cover the fact that he's a sexually attractive, Adonis-looking male and she has...the face that launched a thousand ships. And they're both definitely not blind so come one people, if you put two and two together...yep you got it. They're horny. lol, probably not but that's my guess because i can not understand how a pair of star-crossed lovers turned into a menage minus the sex. Cause that's what it basically was in the last few chapters. <br /><br />Ok, so with the characters... i didn't really like Helen to begin with. I couldn't connect with her or actually anyone in the book. Sure, some parts were funny but all in all, this book never really touched my heart. The world-building was great (apart from the few plotholes), fight scenes were pretty good and I'll give it Josephine that the whole plot was fantastic but the characters lacked a special something that made me fall in love with them. <br /><br />Will I be reading the next book? Yes, i will. I'm actually pretty proud of myself for not skipping to the end and reading what happened because this book was seriously long and confusing as hell at some parts. It is definitely not a good sign when you're reading a book and realise that you are only half way through and you're already struggling.<br /><br />The first thought that came into my head when i finished was "finally.." And can i just say the ending was meh...made me feel sleepy. YOU'RE NOT SUPPOSED TO FEEL SLEEPY AFTER READING THE END. YOU'RE SUPPOSED TO FEEL PUMPED AND EXCITED FOR THE NEXT BOOK. YOUR HEART HAS TO BE RACING AND YOUR BREATHING ACCELERATED AS YOU FLIP THE LAST PAGE AND CLOSE THE BOOK. YOU HAVE TO FEEL LIKE YOU WENT ON A PRIVATE JOURNEY AND EXPERIENCED EMOTIONAL TORTURE AT THE HANDS OF A PAPERBACK. <br />That was a disappointment. <br />All in all, a sound novel but lacking.</span>

<div id="review_272892461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272892461" />
    <a title="Julianna Helms" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5835325-julianna-helms"><img alt="Julianna Helms" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372835701p2/5835325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272892461?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna Helms" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna Helms" href="/user/show/5835325-julianna-helms">Julianna Helms</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Greek mythology and literature</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=re-read-status">re-read-status</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=recent-favorites">recent-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=arc-tours">arc-tours</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=best-boys">best-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272892461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15636059342601526919"><s><b>Quick Reaction:</b> I should make it clear that there are many different ways to judge a book, and I'm judging <i>Dreamless</i> in relativity to Greek myths. Some pet peeves we see abundantly in today's literature are common and incredibly vital to Greek plots, and I must say that in both that aspect and Angelini's soothing narrative, this book certainly deserves 5 stars.<br/><br/>I thought I would hate Orion, but he actually turned out okay. Though Helen annoyed me a bit at some parts, she never crossed the line th</s></span>
  <span id="freeText15636059342601526919" style="display:none"><s><b>Quick Reaction:</b> I should make it clear that there are many different ways to judge a book, and I'm judging <i>Dreamless</i> in relativity to Greek myths. Some pet peeves we see abundantly in today's literature are common and incredibly vital to Greek plots, and I must say that in both that aspect and Angelini's soothing narrative, this book certainly deserves 5 stars.<br /><br />I thought I would hate Orion, but he actually turned out okay. Though Helen annoyed me a bit at some parts, she never crossed the line that made me hate her like <i>Kill Me Softly</i> because at least she was sacrificing for <i>others</i>, instead of being a selfish b-witch.<br /><br />Anywho, this book was just fantastic. It's gripping and quite addictive and, honestly, filled with tension that Greek fans are sure to fall head-over-heels in love with.</s><br /><br /><b>Actual, full review:</b> This review has been scheduled to post on <a href="http://thereviewsnews.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a> on 5/15/2012. Here it is, specially early for Goodreads followers and friends! :D (Note: due to copy-and-paste, formatting and links have been lost.)<br /><br />Josephine Angelini has the uncanny ability to tread uncharted waters and come back with loads of gold in her hands. In other words: what was an aggravating tale of insatiable love, a tale that spanned centuries with infamy and worship--the epic of Helen and Paris, has been transformed completely by Josephine Angelini into an addicting series gleaming with beauty.<br /><br /><br />It has been established, hopefully, that I am as big of a Greek mythology fanatic as they come, and I am not the first to say that this book is not for everyone. It's entertaining and fascinating, of course, but the true core of this novel lies within its ability to reincarnate lost characters into ones radiating with compassion and believability. For fellow geeks of Greek mythology, and others who yearn for a world fastened with gods and weaved with power, Dreamless captures and re-captures the fulfillment of that wish numerous times.<br /><br />This book is obsessive and gorgeous. I just couldn't stop reading it; it was as if I myself was stuck within the lines smothered between words, trying to claw my way out of Helen and Lucas's mesmerizing world yet failing to do so without much care at all. It's Josie's prose, I think, that makes this book such a gripping one: she tells you everything you want to know, but the characters don't know it, and you're just sitting there waiting for them to just freakin' wake up already and see. But it's not the type of frustration that results from annoyance: it's a frustration comprised of your own desires as well as the characters; a concoction that truly glues the reader to the page, I believe.<br /><br />Before I wrap up this review, let's talk about Orion. Ah, yes, Orion: the boy I hated from the moment I read the summary--how could I not, when Helen and Lucas's love was so fragile and so, therefore, also beautiful? But within pages of meeting him, I couldn't help but understand Helen's attraction to Orion as well, for Orion is a charismatic boy who tries so hard to help everyone else; he's altruistically brave, but he's not stupid, and he's understanding as well. So I must say that, even if you believe in Helen and Lucas's love ferociously and fiercely, please don't let it deter you from opening your eyes to try and understand. It's difficult, but I believe that there are roads you never would've seen once you let Josie carry you away in her words.<br /><br />Greek mythology has constructed a vital and irreplaceable contribution to our very society and government, no matter where in the world you are; Josephine Angelini is a storyteller mastering the YA mythological world, and wherever we travel with her next, I know the ride will be as at ease and thrilling as one could dare to dream.<br /><br />P.S. Check out <a href="http://thereviewsnews.blogspot.com/2012/03/starcrossed.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> of the first book in the trilogy, Starcrossed! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15636059342601526919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
